Telegrams by Telephone Implemented the Night Before Last; Trial Run for Three Months Achieved Excellent Results; Projected Increase in Business of One-Fifth

The Shanghai Telegraph Bureau of the Ministry of Communications began implementing telegrams by telephone the night before last, with excellent results. According to Xu Baohua, the chief of the General Affairs Section of the bureau, speaking to a reporter from the Central News Agency, the use of telephone telegrams is purely for the convenience of the citizens. After 6:00 PM every night, branch offices in various locations cease operations, and telegrams must be sent to the main office, which is time-consuming and uneconomical. Therefore, after the implementation of this measure, it is expected that business will increase by one-fifth. The plan is currently to be implemented on a trial basis for three months. If the results are good, it will continue to be implemented. When customers send telegrams by telephone, they may either dictate the text or translate it into code themselves. When the bureau collects payment in the future, it will also review the telegraphic text together. If there are any errors, they can be corrected without additional charge. Customers can also freely request to send wired or wireless telegrams. Otherwise, the bureau will choose the fastest method to send the telegram.

General Situation of Factories in This City

Due to the economic decline in recent years, the business of factories in Shanghai has gradually become sluggish. According to a recent survey by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, there are a total of 3,618 Chinese and foreign factories in the city, with a total capital of 47,306,950 yuan and a workforce of 300,575 people. Details are as follows:

Total Number of Factories

The total number of Chinese and foreign factories in the city includes 720 in machinery manufacturing and metal products manufacturing, 690 textile factories, 105 chemical industries, 215 wood manufacturing factories, 169 metallurgical factories, 46 furniture factories, 416 transportation equipment manufacturing factories, 344 clothing manufacturing factories, 78 rubber factories, 84 food and beverage manufacturing factories, 71 instrument and ornament manufacturing factories, 31 building construction and materials factories, and over 600 other manufacturing factories, totaling 3,618 factories in the city.

Total Capital

Regarding factory capital, textile factories (including cotton spinning factories, silk spinning factories, and wool weaving and dyeing factories) rank first, with 25,964,090 yuan, accounting for nearly half of the total amount. Others include 10,000,360 yuan for the timber industry, 7,673,000 yuan for statue manufacturing factories, 326,100 yuan for metallurgy, 20,074,525 yuan for machinery manufacturing, 10,010,500 yuan for metal products manufacturing, 5,004,400 yuan for power industry, 6,518,250 yuan for transportation equipment manufacturing, 867,700 yuan for earth and stone manufacturing, 11,000,480 yuan for building construction and materials, 10,072,370 yuan for chemical industry, 5,997,500 yuan for clothing manufacturing, 4,549,800 yuan for rubber, 3,333,400 yuan for food and beverage manufacturing, 2,457,550 yuan for printing factories, 15,692,200 yuan for instrument manufacturing, and 1,361,260 yuan for other industries, totaling a total capital of 47,306,950 yuan.

Total Workforce

Regarding the number of workers, there are 4,101 in timber manufacturing, 3,224 in metallurgy, 16,708 in machinery and metal products manufacturing, 73,448 in transportation equipment manufacturing, 3,376 in earth and stone manufacturing, 1,796 in building construction and materials, 5,267 in power industry, 7,426 in chemical industry, and in the textile industry: (a) 74,116 in cotton spinning and weaving, (b) 30,075 in silk spinning and weaving, (c) 6,361 in wool weaving and dyeing, etc., 16,826 in clothing manufacturing, 11,845 in rubber, 1,779 in ornament manufacturing, 13,981 in paper making and printing factories, 32,379 in food and beverage manufacturing, and 4,042 in other industries, totaling 300,575 workers (including male workers, female workers, and child labor) in Chinese and foreign factories in the city.

Banks and Money Houses Prepare to Replenish Funds; Maximize Commercial Lending; Support Industrial and Commercial Development of Production and Business; Revival of the City's Future is Very Promising

According to the Xinxin News Agency, since the Ministry of Finance implemented the reform of the currency system and centralized the issuance of reserves, the financial situation in Shanghai has become more active compared to before November 4th. According to the inspection results of the Issuance Reserve Management Committee, the cash reserves of each issuing bank in Shanghai are on average above 70%, which is quite sufficient. Other non-issuing banks, as well as large and small money houses, have followed the Ministry's order and exchanged legal tender with the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications at a rate of 60% cash and 40% bonds. Therefore, the financial sector can cope with the mutual turnover of funds with ease. It is learned from the banking sector that the banks and money houses in this city are secure themselves, and to promote the prosperity of the market, they should maximize lending to industrial and commercial sectors to maintain industrial and commercial development and production. Therefore, in recent days, banks and money houses have been engaging in commercial lending to sound factories and shops, and the situation is quite good. The future of the city's revival is very promising.

Petition of Salt Farmers in Yuyao Yesterday

According to the Datong News Agency, all the official salt farms in Yuyao, Zhejiang Province, have a total of 507,040 salt pans, making it the most famous salt-producing area in Jiangnan. Recently, under the pretext of excessive salt storage, the local salt factories have announced a temporary suspension of salt collection. The salt farmers have been petitioning for several months. Subsequently, the Salt Transport Envoy issued a notice ordering manufacturers to collect salt at a 40% discount from October 5th. Details are as follows:

The Salt Farmers' Side

Believing that if this continues, their livelihoods will become unsustainable, they petitioned the government. The salt farmer representatives Shang Cailian, Tu Juxiu, Lu Wenrong, Shen Chengzhao, Wang Xizheng, and six others arrived in Shanghai from Yuyao on the morning of the day before yesterday. In the afternoon, they petitioned the Shaoxing Fellow Townsmen Association in Shanghai on Avenue Edward VII, requesting assistance. At 10:00 AM yesterday, they presented a petition to Zhu Tingqi, the Director-General of the Salt Revenue Inspection Office of the Ministry of Finance at No. 18 The Bund. Feng Ruliang, the Chief Inspector, met with them on Zhu's behalf, listened to the salt farmers' complaints, and promised to relay the information to Director-General Zhu for appropriate action. He accepted the petition, and the representatives then took their leave.

The Petition

We, the salt farmers of Yuyao salt farms, numbering approximately 100,000, have always made salt as our profession, living in peace and harmony. However, this spring, the two major salt merchants in eastern and western Zhejiang formed an association in Hangzhou and secretly made an alliance to link transportation areas to greatly suppress salt prices. Because suppressing prices was not enough, they deliberately refused to collect salt, disregarding the lives of the salt farmers. For several months, the people have been cut off from their livelihood and have repeatedly appealed to all parties to petition. Unexpectedly, Commissioner Zhou only listened to the salt merchants and hastily issued a notice on October 5th of this year ordering salt to be collected at a 40% discount. The people were even more alarmed and continued to appeal by letter and telegram, but the salt merchants were powerful and influential, and there was no result. Pitiful are we

Weak and Small Salt Farmers

Crying to heaven but receiving no response, banging our heads on the ground but finding no spirit. In order to prevent the salt merchants from exploiting the salt farmers, the government has established restrictions. Each pan is required to produce 381 catties per year (formerly known as 300 catties), and full payment must be made, with no shortage on either side. This has been a fixed rule for sixty years and has never been changed (omitted). Reducing the amount of salt by 40% would allow the salt farmers to freely transport it to the tax collection points for sales after paying taxes, so the salt farmers' livelihoods could still be maintained. If we allow the salt merchants to slaughter us to fulfill their desires, then in a few years, there will be no salt farmers left. Now we are suffering from hunger and cold, and there is no way to appeal. We have specially sent representatives to visit your esteemed director and petition, to submit everything and attach a written statement of reasons. We respectfully request your kindness to provide relief and strictly order the abolition of the evil precedent of a 40% reduction in quota, and still collect salt at the full amount according to the regulations, in order to save the people's lives and maintain national taxes. We are eagerly awaiting your orders. Presented to Director-General and Chief Inspector Feng of the Salt Revenue Inspection Office of the Ministry of Finance.

Due to Lack of Raw Materials, More Silk Factories Stop Production; Only Twenty Factories Currently Operating

According to the Dagong News Agency, since summer, due to the recovery of foreign sales of raw silk in China, the factories that had stopped production have resumed operations one after another, totaling more than forty. There was a great resurgence in sight. However, before two months had passed, due to the lack of raw materials, they were forced to stop production one after another. It is estimated that the ones that have stopped operating, are Yingfeng, Yutai, Xieyuan, Yuanyu, Yuanji, Yongji, Gengtai, Youli, and Houji in the Zhabei and Xinza districts, totaling twelve factories; China, Changji, and Zhengda in the Hongkou district, totaling three factories; and Weida in the concession district, totaling one factory. Yesterday, four more factories in the Hongkou district, Heji, Detai, Fuxing, and Liyuan, stopped production. The Fengtai Factory in the Zhabei district also stopped production for five days due to insufficient raw materials. In total, more than twenty factories have stopped production. Only Meifeng, Jiyu, Xingchang, Fuchang, Jiuji, Jingcheng, Hengshen, Hongchang, Huixue, Qinyi, Xinchang, Hengcang, Yufeng, Yufeng, and Xinglun in the Zhabei and Xinza districts, totaling fifteen factories, are still in operation. Only Yifeng and Fulun (Shuanggong) in the Hongkou district, totaling two factories, and Yihe and Yuyuan in the concession district, totaling two factories, and Baotai in the Hunan district, totaling one factory, are still in operation, totaling twenty factories. It is heard that there is still a risk of continuous closures in the coming days.

Pacific Union Association Hosted a Lecture by the Soviet Ambassador Yesterday.

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, at noon yesterday, the Pacific Union Association of this city hosted a lecture by Soviet Ambassador Bogomolov at the Astor House Hotel. Among those present were Chinese members Wu Liande, Yu Ming, He DeKui, Wang Zhengfu, Zhu Shaoping, Mr. and Mrs. Yang Guangxing, Mr. and Mrs. Chen Xiangtao, as well as ministers, consuls-general, commercial counselors, business leaders from various countries, totaling more than 200 people. The Vice President of the Association, Guo Bingwen, presided over the meeting and gave an introductory speech, stating that during the final stage of the European War, a great revolution occurred in Russia, and the Soviet government was established. In the shortest period of time, it achieved great success, attracting the great attention of scholars, politicians, and business leaders from all countries. In terms of politics, it established a solid government with its new ideas, courage, and perseverance. In terms of industry, the first five-year plan has been successfully completed, and the second five-year plan will be completed within two years. In terms of education, the illiteracy rate, which used to be 75%, has been eliminated, and all school-age children are now enrolled in school. In terms of diplomacy, it has regained its former position in the international community. Its various successes are truly admirable, and so on. Then, Ambassador Bogomolov delivered a lecture titled "Civil Rights and Culture in the Soviet Union," elaborating in detail on the country's current political situation and cultural status, lasting for a long time. At the end, the chairman gave a speech of thanks, and reported on the association's affairs in the past month before the meeting dispersed.

Health Bureau Issues Notice: Strictly Prohibiting the Extortion of Money and Goods from Those Quitting Opium. All Five Opium Cessation Institutions Are Free of Charge.

The Municipal Health Bureau issued a notice yesterday morning stating: It has been found that the opium cessation institutions established in this city, including the Municipal Hubei Opium Cessation Hospital, the Municipal Hubei Opium Cessation Hospital, the Municipal Temporary Drug Rehabilitation Center, and the Municipal Prisoner Opium Cessation Hospital, are all free of charge for those undergoing opium cessation, and do not charge a single penny. Recently, it has been heard that some people are swindling and defrauding people of their money. In addition to secretly investigating and dealing with this, a notice is hereby issued, urging all those undergoing opium cessation and their families to be aware that if anyone falsely claims to be acting on behalf of the institutions and extorts money or goods, they should be immediately handed over to the police, and a report should be made to this bureau for referral to the authorities for handling. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Instructs on Doubts Regarding Stamp Duty on Returned Goods Slips

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to Nanyang Candle and Soap Factory yesterday, instructing on doubts regarding stamp duty on returned goods slips, stating: "We received your letter of the 21st of this month, inquiring whether stamp duty should be affixed to returned goods slips. The Chamber had previously received a similar inquiry from another business and forwarded it to the Ministry of Finance for instructions. The Ministry of Finance replied that there is no explicit provision in the stamp tax law regarding stamp duty on returned goods slips, so it is not necessary to affix stamp duty. However, if the business, after receiving the returned goods, affixes its store stamp on the returned goods slip and returns the slip to the person returning the goods as proof that the returned goods have been received, then it becomes a receipt for goods under Article 16, Section 2, of the Stamp Tax Law, and stamp duty should be affixed accordingly, and it cannot be considered a returned goods slip. The returned goods slip is the responsibility of the person returning the goods, and the slip is also kept by the store to which the goods are returned. If the store receiving the returned goods affixes its stamp and returns it to the person returning the goods, then the nature of the slip has indeed changed to a receipt. The distinction lies in this point, and your factory should handle it carefully when using it, etc."

Hua Yang Yi Zhen Hui's Relief Efforts in Hubei Province Reportedly Completed in Tianmen, Currently Inspecting Relief Efforts in Zhongxiang

The Renji Road Hua Yang Yi Zhen Hui (Chinese and Foreign Relief Association) believes that the number of relief workers for this disaster in Guangdong and Guangxi is relatively small. Statistics show that there are a total of 5,717 households in the first district, with 223,59 large mouths and 103,18 small mouths. A total of 275 stones and 1.8 dou of rice and beans were distributed in this district. There are 38,52 households in the eighth district, with 157,58 large mouths and 28,00 small mouths. It has been found that the disaster area in the county is extremely scattered, and transportation is very inconvenient. Moreover, the season has reached winter. We are working quickly with Captain Hu and the members of the Red Swastika Society to provide urgent relief to save the people from their suffering. It has been found that the county is divided into ten districts, with the first, second, sixth, and ninth districts being the most severely affected. The first and second districts are the worst, with houses and fields washed away by the water everywhere. It is truly unbearable to witness.

Wang Yangshan Detained by Police for Buying Silver Dollars.

Wang Yangshan, a Zhenjiang native who has been engaged in the money business, recently took advantage of the government's implementation of the paper currency policy to travel around the southern city every day, buying silver dollars from shops and residents, and stipulating that 100 silver dollars could be exchanged for 107 yuan in paper money. The day before yesterday evening, Wang was asking a shopkeeper in Xiaodongmen if he had silver dollars to exchange for paper money, but he was overheard by a patrol officer, who immediately stepped forward to arrest him. 329 yuan in paper money prepared for buying silver dollars was found on Wang's person. He was immediately taken to the Yemiao Police Station under the jurisdiction, where Director Liu interrogated him. Wang confessed that he was 35 years old and lived at 24 Yuqingli, outside Xiaobeimen. He used to work as a clerk in a money shop. He stammered about why he passed Xiaodongmen. Because the case involved buying silver dollars, violating the government's ban, he was ordered to prepare a document and send it to the General Bureau for interrogation.

Armed Clashes Between Police and Bandits Occurred Near Jinghu Road's Huangdu for Consecutive Nights. Six Bandits Attempted to Rob Road Police of Firearms. Two Road Police Shot and Wounded, but Their Lives Are Not in Danger.

The Jinghu Road (Shanghai-Nanjing Railway) is the only main line for entering and exiting the capital. At ordinary times, officials and dignitaries from China and abroad pass by in an endless stream. In order to maintain the safety of traffic, the road authorities recently organized a joint patrol of industrial police, relaying road signs along the entire line every night without stopping, and the defense can be said to be very tight. However, on the nights of the 20th and 21st, bandits were found near Huangdu Station on the road, engaging in armed clashes with the road police, resulting in one road policeman being shot and wounded. As this concerns the safety of the railway, the detailed information obtained is recorded as follows:

Searching the Road at Night

Police and Bandits Clash

At about 8:00 p.m. on the 20th, Zhao Xuemin, a road patrol police officer near the 25-kilometer mark of Huangdu Station, was patrolling the road when he suddenly encountered six bandits. Two of them were each holding a box cannon, and all were wearing blue cloth short jackets and trousers. One of the bandits first spoke in a northern accent, asking the police officer what he was doing, and then ordered him to surrender his gun. The police officer knew that he had encountered bandits and quickly opened fire. The two sides then engaged in a fight. The police officer was shot twice and ran out of bullets. He was then hugged around the waist by a bandit. The police officer struggled desperately and threw his gun into the muddy ditch beside the road.

Military Police Join the Arrest

No Trace of Bandits

At that moment, a night train passed by, and the police officer blew his whistle frantically. The bandits failed to find the gun and fled with shouts. After a while, the Huangdu police and the security team of military police received the alarm and rushed to assist. They saw Officer Zhao lying in a pool of blood. They immediately provided emergency treatment and sent him to the station to take a train to Shanghai for treatment. At the same time, they searched for the bandits and pursued them in all directions. At about 9:00 p.m., Zhong Jianhun, the section chief of the Shanghai North Station Road Police Section, received a report and immediately dispatched several armed police officers, opened a special police car and rushed to the scene, and joined the military police to encircle and arrest them. He also personally went to contact the local garrison and surrounded all the nearby villages on all sides. Early in the morning of the 21st, he entered the villages to search, but found nothing. The police officers dispatched that night to block the bandits along the Shanghai-Xiangshan line also reported the next morning that they had not found any trace of the bandits.

Wounded Police Officer Out of Danger

Lost Gun Recovered

After being sent to the Two Roads Hospital, the wounded police officer Zhao Xuemin's injuries did not change. He was shot twice, once in the left arm and once in the right leg, but his life was not in danger. It is heard that the police officer is a native of Wuzhou, Guangxi, and is 27 years old. He served as a squad leader in the Seventh Army and has extraordinary strength. Therefore, this time he fought against six bandits and was not harmed. It has been found that the pistol thrown into the mud ditch by the police officer at the time has been recovered. Therefore, the road police section chiefs have praised the police officer's brave road protection. The strength of the Huangdu area has also been increased in order to eliminate bandit police incidents at any time.

Bandits Reappear

Security Remains Tight

It was learned that at 12:30 a.m. on the 21st, bandits were still found in the Huangdu area the night before, and there were gunshots fired by bandits at the original location. Fortunately, the police and military police stationed there immediately concentrated and fired back. The bandits were unable to succeed. It has been found that the Jinghu Road has always been peaceful, but in recent years, due to the bankruptcy of the rural economy, bandits have proliferated and there is unrest everywhere. Now, in order to curb the source of the disaster, the road police affairs section has, in addition to increasing police force, also informed the elders and village chiefs along the line that if they encounter anyone with suspicious behavior or speaking with a foreign accent, they should immediately report it in order to eliminate the source of the bandits.

Foreign Monk Zhao Kong Sues Russian Newspaper for Defamation, Requesting Compensation of 10,000 Yuan Due to Publication of His Biography.

Stateless Buddhist foreign monk Zhao Kong, originally named Szelo Berchol Lincoln, 57 years old this year, originally from Hungary, has been residing in Shanghai recently, lecturing and teaching, and promoting Buddhism. The Russian Zira Evening News (located in the Russian Trust Bank branch building) at 774 Avenue Joffre in this city published a news item on August 3 this year, which stated that Szelo Berchol Lincoln served as a military detective in Abyssinia, supplied military weapons, that he was the son of a poor Polish merchant, that he was formerly a Lutheran pastor in Hamburg, Germany, and finally came to China as a monk, and became a Buddhist, that after the European War, he had nowhere to stay in Europe, and went to India to help the Bolshevik Party work, inciting peace in the Far East, etc. After Zhao Kong read it, he believed that the newspaper published this item without reason, intending to damage his reputation. Therefore, he hired Russian lawyer Shu Shengni to file a complaint, accusing the manager of Zira Evening News, Russian Li Biqi, and the editor, Russian Weis (said to be female), of defamation under Article 310, Section 2 of the Criminal Code in the Second Special Court's Criminal Division, requesting that they be investigated according to law, and incidentally filing a civil lawsuit, requesting that the defendants be ordered to compensate for losses of 10,000 yuan, etc. According to the complaint, the court, at 10:00 a.m. yesterday, ordered a summons by Judge Sun Penghuan from Criminal Division 2. The plaintiff appeared through his lawyer, and there was a disciple of Zhao Kong who spoke French, wore a Chinese monk's robe, and had incense scars on his head, who went to the court to listen to the trial. The defendants appeared through Chinese lawyer Jiang Guofang, stating that defendant Li Biqi was ill, and Weis was sleeping in the morning due to her editing duties and work in the evening, so she did not appear in court. Therefore, the plaintiff's lawyer stated the purpose of the lawsuit, stating that the article published by Zira Evening News had 12 points that defamed the plaintiff's reputation, requesting an investigation, etc. The defendant's lawyer stated that the defendants did not maliciously publish this article, but reprinted it from a Latvian French newspaper published in Geneva. Before publishing this article, the plaintiff had been to the newspaper office and talked about his impending retirement. Later, the newspaper saw this bizarre article and found it very strange, so it reprinted it and added an explanation, stating that they had seen the Zhao Kong monk in Shanghai a week ago, which was beneficial to the plaintiff. At this point, the court, because both parties had not appeared in court, ordered both lawyers to inform their clients that they must appear in court themselves at the next hearing and adjourned the hearing to 9:30 a.m. on the 29th of this month for further questioning.

Winter Rainstorm, Strange Yangtze River Flooding Event, Rare in 20 Years, Two Vessels Caused Trouble Due to Tidal Surge, Large Quantities of Grain Being Transported

Since the 16th of this month, heavy rains have been continuous in the upper and lower reaches of the Yangtze River, followed by rainstorms. In previous years, by mid-November, the water level of the upper reaches of the Yangtze River had greatly decreased, and large-scale river vessels could no longer navigate to ports such as Shashi, Yichang, Chongqing, and Changsha, but could only switch to shallow-draft vessels. This was the so-called dry season. This year is very different. In the past week, the water level has been rising instead of decreasing due to the combined effects of heavy rain and rainstorms. This is a rare event that has not been seen in 20 years, and ocean liners can still navigate to the upper reaches.

Vessels Cause Trouble

Due to the continuous heavy rains in the Yangtze River, commercial vessels have caused trouble. The Xing Shi vessel of the Sanbei Company, which has a very large tonnage and a deep draft, is usually difficult to navigate in the Xiangjiang River. This time, it sailed from Changsha to Jiujiang and arrived at Xunpu on the 19th. Just as it was raining heavily and windy, it wanted to dock at the China Merchants Wharf and damaged the pontoon boat, which was caused by the impact of the wind and rain. In addition, the Songpu vessel damaged a lightship set up by the Jianghan Customs at the Cement Channel, also due to the impact of the rainstorm. Fortunately, the damage was minor, so compensation was paid and the matter was settled.

Grain Transportation

The transportation of grain on the Yangtze River was suspended for a few days. Recently, grain merchants have telegraphed for large quantities to be loaded in Shanghai. Therefore, since the 21st of this month, they have been rushing to load. The Songpu vessel is heading east with a huge amount of rice, wheat, and miscellaneous grains loaded. Other companies' Yangtze River vessels are also starting to load grain. Within the next three or four days, a large amount of grain will be transported to Shanghai.

According to Xin Xin News Agency, Sanbei, Ningshao, Dada, Datong, Pingan, Daxing, Hezong, Maoli, Lian'an, Huxing, Ruian, Jufeng, Chongming, and other shipping companies in this city, in view of the arrival of winter and the prevalence of pirates, in order to maintain navigation and protect the safety of passengers, have met and decided to implement winter precautions early in accordance with past practice, ending at the end of March next year. During the winter precaution period, it was decided to contact the Public Security Bureau to increase armed police patrols at the docks and dispatch undercover agents to inspect suspicious passengers before the vessels set sail to prevent pirates from entering. All expenses will be shared by the shipping companies.

Guangdong Rubber Factory Dispute Resolved Through Party Mediation: Eight-Point Settlement Agreement Signed, Party Headquarters Issues Notice for Work Resumption

According to Da Gong She, all workers of the Guangdong Brothers Rubber Factory on Peikai'er Road, Hongkou, went on strike last month due to a wage arrears dispute with the factory management. The issue remained unresolved after many days. The Municipal Party Headquarters specially convened a meeting of both labor and management yesterday morning to mediate, and an eight-point resolution agreement was signed. The Party Headquarters issued a notice to the workers to return to work uniformly on the 26th. The details are recorded below:

Resolution Methods

The Municipal Party Headquarters convened a meeting of both labor and management of the factory at 10:00 AM yesterday to mediate. The factory was represented by Wei Jianqiu and Gan Junzhe, while the labor was represented by Liu Zhongying and Luo Yuan'ao. The meeting was presided over by Lu Yinchu, a cadre from the Civil Movement Section of the Municipal Party Headquarters. After repeated persuasion from both sides, an eight-point resolution method was signed: (1) The wages for July will be paid in full within nine days after work resumes. If the wages for July have already been paid, new wages will be paid on the day after work resumes. (2) After the wages for July are paid, the wages for November will be paid within six days. All subsequent wages will be paid on the day after work is completed. The remaining fifteen days' wages will be the responsibility of the factory representative. (3) After the workers resume work, if there are indeed unavoidable circumstances that require them to return home, the factory will issue wages for August, September, and October, but limited to one person per day. (4) The workers' representatives will legally pursue the owed wages for September and October through the court. If all creditors agree to a settlement, the labor side must also agree to the settlement, but the capital side must respond to the labor side within 20 days. (5) All workers must return to work on November 26th. (6) Cancel entry and exit permits; workers can enter the factory with their work passbooks. (7) The wage slips for October will be issued immediately. (8) The factory must not dismiss workers without cause.

Notice of Resumption of Work

The Shanghai Special Municipal Party Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang issued a notice stating that regarding the labor dispute of Guangdong Brothers Rubber Company, the committee convened both labor and management to the meeting on the 21st of this month to mediate and agreed on eight settlement methods on the spot. All workers of the company are hereby notified to comply with the regulations and return to work at the factory uniformly on the 26th of this month without delay. This is a firm notice. Standing Committee Members: Pan Gongzhan, Wu Xingya, and Tong Xingbai.

Yesterday, the Local Court Continued Hearing Chang Junfa Describe Scenes of Fraud

Salted fish merchants Weng Zhaofang, Ye Zhenchang, Zheng Yunsheng, Zhang Benhua, Ye Zhenqin, etc., were recently sued by Zhu Xusheng, Chang Junfa, Zhao Lianfang, etc., to the Procuratorate of the Local Court, confessing that Weng, etc., fraudulently obtained money and evaded national taxes. They took advantage of the opportunity of various fish shops to order 50,000 dan of salmon from Suwo Helping Society foreign company, and took the opportunity to instigate the confessors and eight trained small workers to cheat during the weighing process, stealing a total of 6,700 dan, worth more than 70,000 yuan. The prosecutor Lei Binzhang conducted a clear investigation and prosecuted the Criminal Court under Article 339, Paragraph 2. Judge Wu Deying has held several joint trials, but the case has not been concluded due to its complexity. The details have been recorded in previous reports. It is now known that this case was reopened by Judge Wu in the third court at 2:00 PM yesterday for further hearing. The defendants Weng Zhaofang, etc., and the confessors Zhu Xusheng, etc., all complied with the summons to appear in court. The judge briefly questioned each defendant, and then Zhu Xusheng testified that the manifest of the goods was copied by Zhang Benhua. When Zhang Benhua was questioned, he flatly denied it. The judge ordered Zhang Benhua to copy the manifest in court in order to verify the handwriting. Then, Chang Junfa testified that he was a small foreman at the wharf and was instructed by Mr. Ye to summon 32 small workers, totaling 16 carriers, divided into four holds, with four carriers in each hold, and each carrier carrying three boxes of salmon. If each carrier weighed 360 to 370 pounds, if cheating occurred, the weight would be reduced to only 300 pounds or so. When Chang Junfa testified, he described the situation of cheating at that time in great detail. The judge obtained the confession, and for the sake of caution, he still needs to summon witnesses for a joint interrogation and verification. Therefore, the court adjourned.

Immoral Monk and Lecherous Woman's No Small Offense: Guanyin Temple Visit to Delightful Meditation, Admission of Three Years of Commuting Unashamedly, Immoral Monk Sentenced to Five Months, Lecherous Woman Detained for Three Months

Ren Ci, a monk of Guanyin Temple on Ou Jia Road, originally from Jiangbei, with the secular name Chen Ruhai, is only 30 years old. Not only are his six senses not exhausted, but his blood is also very vigorous. As the Shanghai dialect says, there are so-called "flowery monks" who, in addition to chanting scriptures and worshiping Buddha, are also good at singing various lewd and vulgar songs in the Jiangbei tune. These flowery monks often seek a smile from benefactors, and after chanting scriptures, they sing "Jiangbei Capturing Zhang Sanlang Alive," which can be said to be extremely unethical. And Ren Ci is indeed of the same ilk as the flowery monks, with a frivolous demeanor and a great love for women. When Guanyin Temple was formerly located in Xinyi Lane, Xujiahui Road, it was adjacent to Jin, the wife of Li Jiushan, a fellow villager, who was inherently lewd. After the monk slightly seduced her, she formed an intimate relationship with him, and often took the opportunity to go to the monk's room to visit Delightful Meditation. Later, when the temple moved to its current location, Jin was still passionate about the affair. She waited for Li to go out, no matter how late, and went to meet him secretly. Ren Ci was originally a poor monk, wearing straw sandals and a patchwork robe, and his face was covered with pockmarks, but Jin did not hesitate to condescend and did not care about her husband's labor (Li was a rickshaw puller). Seeing that Li had wages and bought rice, she would definitely find a way to carry the rice and money to the temple to fulfill her wish to provide for the monk and to fulfill the appointment of Sangpu. This kind of action has been going on for three years. Recently, Li finally heard about it, and because he was unwilling to wear a green hat for a long time, he decided to deal with it. Coincidentally, Jin left home again the night before last. Li waited until midnight but still did not see her return, so he reported to the Jiaxing Road Police Station and sent detective Wang Jinshou to rush to the temple with Li. It was early morning, and the pair of wild mandarin ducks were still sound asleep. Wang and other detectives suddenly broke into the room, and they were startled awake, but there was no way to escape. They had no choice but to put on their clothes and be bound. Wang and other detectives searched the room and found a photo of Ren Ci and Jin together, and took them back to the police station together, separately detaining them until yesterday morning, when they were sent to the First Special District Local Court. Judge Zhan Liangce interrogated them, and the police lawyer Jiang Baolian filed a complaint of adultery, requesting punishment according to Article 239 of the Criminal Law. When the two defendants were questioned, they bowed their heads and admitted that they had been having an affair for three years. Judge Zhan interrogated them and sentenced Ren Ci to five months in prison and Li Jin to three months in prison as a warning.

Rent Dispute in Lishui Lane, Danshui Road Involves Litigation, Landlord and Tenant Hold Conflicting Views

The lawyer Tao Wuzhi, from Suzhou, and his rent collector Pan Qipeng, were recently privately prosecuted by Zheng Haiting, a Cantonese tenant, for forging documents and defaming his reputation in the Criminal Division of the Special No. 2 Court, with a lawyer representing him. After Judge Li Changnian of the Special No. 2 Court opened a court session to summon them, Tao and Pan not only submitted a defense but also filed a counterclaim for false accusation and defamation, requesting the court to order the defendant in the counterclaim to compensate them for their loss of reputation by one yuan each and to publish an apology to restore their reputation. After the hearing, it was rescheduled for another hearing. It has already been recorded in this newspaper. The day before yesterday afternoon, Judge Li opened the court again for a continued hearing. The private prosecutor Zheng Haiting, because he did not understand the Shanghai dialect, went to court with his son Zheng Xiaofeng and his representing lawyer. The defendants also went to court with their defense lawyer, Zhang Shizhao. First, the private prosecutor said that he had rented a house at No. 11 Lishui Lane, Danshui Road for many years, and the rent was 52 yuan per month. At the end of last year, the landlord wanted to renovate the house, and the tenants asked to extend the lease and increase the rent to 67 yuan. Because I thought the amount was too expensive and not worth it, I verbally agreed to find a house to move out and not participate in the tenants' group, so I did not sign a contract with the defendants. Later, in mid-April of this year, I found a house and paid off the rent and moved out. The other tenants agreed to increase the rent to 67 yuan and signed a contract. They also signed a separate contract for repaying half a month's rent each month. Later, the defendant suddenly filed a lawsuit in your court's Civil Division, accusing me of owing rent. The first trial failed, and the appeal to the High Sub-Court suddenly produced a contract as evidence. Pan Qipeng also went to court to give false testimony, saying that I had signed this contract and that I had moved privately. I did not sign this contract. It was obviously forged by the defendants. Saying that I moved privately was intentional to damage my reputation. When I moved, I hired Zhongfu Moving Company, from 8:00 AM to 4:00 or 5:00 PM, making three or four trips back and forth. At 11:00 AM that day, Pan Qipeng came, and I returned the key to him. Moreover, there was a caretaker in the lane, how could I move privately? I request an investigation, etc. Tao Wuzhi testified that all 23 tenants signed contracts. The private prosecutor had fulfilled the new rent for four months and paid the new rent, so he gave him the new rent tickets for January to April. The old rent had not been paid from September to December. Because he moved privately, he filed a lawsuit to recover the rent. This contract was written by the private prosecutor and handed over to the rent collector to bring back. In the beginning, the blank contract was written in the first paragraph by the rental office and handed over to the rent collector to be distributed to the tenants to sign and stamp on the back themselves. He also presented the contracts of all the tenants as evidence. He also testified that the private prosecutor made false accusations and requested a clear judgment to allow the counterclaim. Pan Qipeng testified that the contract was sent by me to each tenant. At that time, it was sent to the private prosecutor's place, but the private prosecutor was not at home, so it was sent to the Public Works Bureau and handed to his son. Later, I also collected it from his son. Every month, I went to the Public Works Bureau to collect the room rent from his son. The private prosecutor did not notify me when he moved. He moved out privately and continuously. It was not until the caretaker saw that there was no one in the house and reported to me to watch. The door was closed, and knocking on the door did not answer. He went to the Public Works Bureau to ask the private prosecutor's son, who replied that he had moved out and handed me the key. One day, I went to open the door to look and saw only three old military beds left in the house, and nothing else, etc. The court verified the testimonies, and since both sides held their own ground, it was announced that it would be rescheduled for a further hearing on the 26th.

Grandmother and Granddaughter Poisoned

Grandmother Takes Poison Due to Prolonged Illness, Attempting Suicide, Granddaughter Accidentally Drinks It, Both Suffer Poisoning Simultaneously

Wu Li, a Ningbo woman, 49 years old, lived at No. 103 Yuanji Lane, Tangshan Road. Because she was weak and often ill, she was always near the medicine stove. Therefore, she was very resentful. Recently, she had been ill for a long time and could not get up. She tossed and turned in bed, suffering unspeakable pain, which led to the thought of ending her life. Suddenly, at about 1:00 AM yesterday morning, she privately soaked raw opium in boiling water, added sugar, and drank half a bowl of it, covering herself with a blanket to sleep, hoping to commit suicide. It did not take effect. The woman's granddaughter, Xiaomei, 19 years old, woke up from a nap beside her. Because she was thirsty for a moment, she vaguely saw half a bowl of poisonous substance in the bowl, thinking it was tea, and drank it all in one gulp. Therefore, before long, both the grandmother and granddaughter suffered poisoning at the same time, and screamed for help due to abdominal pain. Fortunately, her family and neighbors heard the screams and came. After learning the situation, they rushed the two to the hospital for treatment. Their condition was very critical.

Shanghai Radio Weekly

Germany's "Decimeter Waves"

— Pao

Due to the development of radio, the number of radio stations is increasing daily. The current wavebands are insufficient for allocation, making it difficult to accommodate new stations. Therefore, ultrashort wavebands between five meters and one meter are gradually being explored and put into practical use. "Decimeter Waves" (referring to radio waves between one-tenth of a meter and one meter) have also been secretly and systematically tested by the German Telefunken Co. in the past one or two years and may be put into practical use in the future.

The wavelength of decimeter waves is less than one meter, so the frequency is as high as 300 million cycles or more. Under this high-frequency current, most of the components in ordinary radio equipment are no longer applicable, so they must be manufactured separately for testing.

The transmitter is also specially designed, and the oscillation tube used is a special "Haban Tube," namely, a split-anode magnetron. The circuit of the transmitter and the internal structure of the Haban tube are shown in Figure A. The tube has a cathode, surrounded by a cylindrical anode split into four pieces (as shown in the upper left corner of Figure A). Two opposing pieces are connected with wires and led out of the tube, as shown by the dotted lines in the figure. In use, the anode is connected to a positive voltage, and a strong electromagnet is placed outside the tube. Electrons emitted from the cathode are attracted to the anode by the anode voltage, while being deflected back to the cathode by the external electromagnet, thus creating oscillation and generating radio waves in the oscillation circuit.

Vacuum tubes in the receiver include triodes and diodes, which are also specially manufactured and extremely small in size to minimize the time electrons spend passing through the vacuum tube. Tests show that these diodes can work satisfactorily even with wavelengths as short as 40 centimeters.

During testing, these decimeter waves were used to guide ships into port, with excellent results. In addition, two sets of transceivers using the same wavelength were able to transmit and receive simultaneously at very close distances, reportedly operating independently without interfering with each other.

Figure B shows a portable decimeter wave transmitter and its reflector. Figure C shows the antenna arrangement for a decimeter wave receiver. Figure D shows the Haban vacuum tube with an electromagnet placed outside.

Overview of Broadcasting Facilities in Europe and America

— Ming

If you want to do a good job, you must first sharpen your tools.

The development of radio in modern times has been rapid. However, to achieve good results and significant effects, attention must be paid not only to the broadcasting equipment and radios, but also to the broadcasting facilities, various equipment, and management systems to achieve perfection. This is beyond doubt.

Now, I will briefly describe the facilities and systems of broadcasting stations in Europe and America. Given the number of broadcasting stations and the popularity of radios in Shanghai, this may serve as a reference.

Broadcasting stations in Europe and America, recognizing that broadcasting equipment and radios have almost reached perfection, have recently shifted their focus to improving broadcasting studio equipment.

The most important aspects of broadcasting studio construction are: First, it must be completely insulated from external sounds and noise. Second, it must maintain good sound quality for sounds produced inside.

To achieve these two goals, major broadcasting stations in Europe and America have made great efforts. Some use two- to four-inch thick asbestos attached to the four walls, floor, and ceiling of the broadcasting studio (such as the N.BC. broadcasting studio in New York, USA), while others use wood blocks (such as the Leipzig broadcasting station in Germany). Some even use hydraulic presses to open and close the doors of the broadcasting studio to appropriately adjust the degree of "reverberation."

As for the structure of broadcasting studios, it varies according to the system. The New World and European countries have different approaches.

In many broadcasting stations in the United States, in addition to broadcasting for listeners to listen to, the public is allowed to enter the broadcasting studio to listen to the broadcast directly. For a ticket costing just four cents, anyone can enter. Therefore, broadcasting studios in the United States can accommodate more than 2,000 direct listeners. Broadcasting studios that can accommodate one or two hundred people are very common. To prevent noise and interference from the audience, these broadcasting studios are often specially enclosed with glass to separate the performance stage, so that the performers' various movements and expressions can be seen but the sound cannot be heard directly. The music performed in the glass room is transmitted to the audience outside the glass room using a special "sound amplifier." This sound amplifier can only transmit the music from the glass room and does not allow noise from the audience outside to enter. Therefore, even with thousands of listeners, the radio broadcast is not affected in any way. It is said that there are about 30 radio broadcasting stations in the United States with this type of glass-enclosed broadcasting studio.

The situation is the opposite in the British dominions. Although they also pay attention to the construction of broadcasting studios and strive to improve them, they generally do not allow people to enter the broadcasting studio to listen directly, except for those with special relationships. Therefore, their broadcasting studios naturally do not need to be built on such a grand scale as those in the United States. As for the glass room in the broadcasting studio, they consider it a "useless object."

As for the power used by broadcasting stations, the United States and Europe are also the opposite.

In the United States, because it is less affected by radio waves from other countries, most broadcasting stations use about 100 watts of power, with more than 600 such stations. Stations with 50 kilowatts or more are rare, with only about 20 such stations nationwide. Recently, Cincinnati has built a powerful 500-kilowatt broadcasting station, but its performance is questionable.

The situation in Europe is the opposite. Because the countries of Europe are connected and close to each other, international broadcasting competition is naturally fierce. Therefore, their broadcasting stations mostly use high power. For example, the Soviet Union has broadcasting stations with 500 kilowatts of power, and about 20 stations with 100 kilowatts or more. France has six or seven broadcasting stations with 100 kilowatts. Italy has also built a 500-kilowatt station to compete. Therefore, the competition for high-power broadcasting is very fierce in Europe.

As for commercial advertising in broadcasting, it is prevalent in the commercial country of the United States. There are even companies specializing in soliciting and negotiating radio advertising. On the European side, advertising broadcasting is rare, and in some cases, nonexistent.

In addition, there are various special broadcasting stations. For example, there is a broadcasting station outside Paris that specializes in broadcasting music that suits the tastes of the British, and most of its listeners are British residents in Britain. Furthermore, Britain, the United States, Germany, Italy, and other countries have established shortwave broadcasting stations to broadcast strongly to their colonies to facilitate their imperialist aggression policies. The colonies of European and American countries are mostly far from their home countries, so ordinary broadcasting stations cannot be effective and strong shortwave broadcasting is necessary.

Electrical Power and Electrical Work

— Enlun

Electric current has a certain working capacity, and the working capacity of the electric current is called electrical energy. The work done by the electric current is called electrical work, and the work done by the electric current per second is called electrical power. Electrical power P is equal to the product of voltage V (volts) and current I (amperes), i.e.,

P = V * I ... (1)

The unit for measuring electrical power is the watt (one watt is the electrical power of one ampere of current at a voltage of one volt). Sometimes multiples of watts are used as larger units of power, such as hectowatts and kilowatts.

1 hectowatt = 100 watts

1 kilowatt = 1000 watts

From equation (1), current I or voltage V can also be obtained from electrical power P.

Ohm's law expresses the relationship between voltage, current, and resistance, and the formula for electrical power expresses the relationship between power, current, and voltage. Both relationships can be represented by a circle, as shown in Figure A for Ohm's law and Figure B for the law of electrical power. (To be continued)

A Visit to the China Alcohol Factory (Continued)

— Huang Youxiong

Alcohol and spirits - The uses of alcohol - The required amount of alcohol in China

The manufacturing of alcohol - A tour of the whole factory - Hopes for the future

(V) A Tour of the Whole Factory

The China Alcohol Factory has its own small steamship to shuttle between Shanghai and Bailianjing to pick up and drop off commissioners and workers. The factory buildings are all built with steel frame and cement, with flat roofs and a magnificent appearance. The factory is divided into three departments: chemical, mechanical, and administrative. The chemical and mechanical departments each have a chief engineer and several assistant managers. The administrative department has Chinese and Western secretaries and several clerks. The total number of mechanics and workers in the factory is only over a hundred, and the factory covers an area of 150 acres, but it can be managed carefully and in an orderly manner. This is certainly due to the complete equipment and the use of machinery for all work, but it also shows the painstaking efforts in planning and design.

The reporters, led by Director Tang himself, first went to the chemical laboratory, which specializes in manufacturing parts of the experiment. Next to it is the culture room and sterilization room, which are responsible for yeast culture. The original yeast is the most important thing in the manufacture of alcohol. The quality of the alcohol produced is closely related to the yeast. Therefore, the factory attaches great importance to it. There are many kinds of yeast, and the room uses glass tubes to store them separately for selection. The factory also requires various raw materials used to undergo small-scale tests before large-scale manufacturing.

Next is the germination room, located on a flat roof covered with glass. Below is the germination tank. The room uses the latest air conditioners, so malt can be produced even when the atmosphere is warm. The purpose of malt is to make the starch in grains and potatoes saccharified.

When grains are used as raw materials to manufacture alcohol, the raw material processing room is extremely important. The room is equipped with a dust removal machine, a dehulling machine, a shell screening machine, and a grinder. Although these are based on the same principles as ordinary rural windmills and mills, the use of modern machinery makes the work faster and more efficient. All transportation uses bag-type or spiral automatic conveyors, eliminating the trouble of manual handling.

Next is the cooking and saccharification room, which mixes grains with malt to saccharify them. It is equipped with high-pressure cooking machines, saccharification machines, and cooling machines. The above rooms are indispensable equipment for manufacturing alcohol using grain starch raw materials. The factory will soon start manufacturing them. When the reporters visited, a large amount of ring bell was placed for storage.

The subsequent visit was to various manufacturing processes using cane molasses as raw material. The factory currently uses molasses imported from Southeast Asia to manufacture alcohol. After the molasses is transported, it is first stored in the storage tank at the factory entrance. When used, it is automatically sent to the dilution room, diluted with water, and stirred evenly with filtered compressed air. The room is equipped with a pure yeast culture device for fermenting grain mash and molasses.

The main process in alcohol manufacturing is fermentation. The factory is equipped with 16 closed fermentation tanks, each with a capacity of 7650 liters. Steam pipes, water pipes, and air pipes are installed inside. Fermentation produces alcohol and carbon dioxide. The carbon dioxide is passed from the top of the tank through a main pipe into the carbon dioxide manufacturing room for the manufacture of dry ice and liquid air.

The reporter stayed in the fermentation room for a while. At that time, fermentation was in progress. When the tank cover was opened, the inside was full of foam, pale yellow, and the smell of alcohol was pungent. The fermentation tanks stand in rows, which is very grand. Each tank is attached with a label, indicating the elapsed time and its temperature, and someone observes it at all times.

Finally, to the distillation room. The distillation machine was made by the British Blair Company and is a continuous distillation refining and purification machine. Engineer Wei told us that when alcohol is distilled, the "head" and "tail" must be separated and purified from the finished product. The so-called head is the alcohol that is initially distilled, which often contains low-boiling aldehydes. The so-called tail is the high-boiling fusel oil that is distilled last. These must be purified, and then the alcohol can be pure and good. The distilled alcohol is then stored in the storage tower outside the storage room.

At this point, the alcohol manufacturing work is completed. Then go downstairs to the canning room to visit. The filling method is generally automatic management, either by volume or by weight, and is very precise and reliable. The factory has storage tanks, each with a capacity of one million liters, which can store about two months of products.

In addition to the above rooms, the factory needs electricity for the operation of various machines. Therefore, it has its own 400-kilowatt generator to supply electricity for all motors and lights in the factory. The factory also needs a large amount of water and steam. Therefore, it has its own well dug 700 feet deep, which can produce 136,500 liters of water per hour. The supply of steam is provided by two water-tube boilers, and the burning of coal and the removal of ash after burning are also done by machinery.

For the safety of the factory, the factory is also equipped with a fire-fighting water pump, driven by a gasoline engine, which can draw 4556 liters of water per minute and can send the water from the Huangpu River to all parts of the factory to prevent fire.

After the visit, the reporter took a photo with Director Tang and expressed his gratitude. He then returned to the hotel by the factory's own steamship. Mr. Wei and Mr. Lin were also able to take the same boat back to Shanghai, and the reporter was able to get the two gentlemen to further explain the working procedures and all the facilities in the factory.

(VI) Hopes for the Future

The China Alcohol Factory has been in operation for only two years since its preparation, and the quality of its products is comparable to that of imported products. Given the urgent need for alcohol in China, it is the most promising business. The reporters' visit, although very brief, did not allow for detailed consultation, but seeing the perfection of its machinery and equipment and the precision of its working procedures is rare in the current industrial world of our country. However, alcohol is a basic raw material for the chemical industry, and it can be as important as acids and bases. The more developed a country's industry is, the more alcohol it needs. If our country's industry continues to develop, the current output of the China Alcohol Factory may still be insufficient to meet the demand, and it needs to be expanded again. Fortunately, the factory has already left room for expansion, which is very easy. In the future, we only hope that the Chinese people can know that China already has domestically produced alcohol and use it consistently, so that the outflow of rights can be avoided.

The China Alcohol Factory currently uses molasses as raw material. The factory has equipment for making alcohol from grains, and grains and potatoes are produced everywhere in our country. In the future, we hope to actively develop, so that all raw materials are made of domestic goods. Not only will the rights not be leaked out, but agricultural products can also have a way out.

Finally, our country has few domestic liquid fuels, and the need for liquid fuels is increasing day by day. Alcohol can replace gasoline, and various countries have proven its success, but its combination components still have room for research. We also hope that the people of the country can rise up and promote and research it, so that its benefits for national defense and transportation cannot be exhausted in one word. (The End)

Children's Year: Center Develops Teaching Outline

Education Bureau Will Issue to All Elementary School Teachers for Earnest Study and Submission to the Elementary Education Research Association for Discussion Before Implementation

The Municipal Education Bureau yesterday instructed the chairpersons of the municipal elementary schools, private registered elementary schools, and district elementary education research associations: "Based on a report submitted by Zhu Xiaolin of Lingqiao Elementary School stating that Children's Year, advocated by the Shanghai Children's Happiness Committee, the Chinese Orphanage Association, and others, has been formally mandated by the National Government and commenced on August 1st, and that schools are the second home of children, in order to genuinely promote children's welfare, a teaching outline centered on Children's Year should be formulated and implemented, and that the bureau should stipulate that meetings and exhibitions be held around Children's Day next year for strict review, to serve as an important part of this year's performance evaluation. The school requests that the teaching outline be drafted by outstanding elementary schools or jointly prepared by district education research groups to gather diverse perspectives. The school has prepared a draft of the Children's Year teaching outline and respectfully submits it for review and implementation. After review, the request to instruct all elementary schools to implement a school program centered on Children's Year is feasible. Apart from revising the original draft and scheduling a citywide exhibition of elementary schools' Children's Year teaching achievements, and issuing relevant notices, the draft is hereby publicly announced for all elementary school teachers to thoroughly study and provide opinions to their respective district elementary education research associations. Following the second general meeting of this year, the district elementary research association chairpersons shall submit the discussion results to this bureau for submission to the citywide elementary education research association for final review, in order to ensure smooth implementation and promotion. The attached Children's Year teaching outline draft is as follows:

(1) Introduction: This year is Children's Year, and its significance directly involves increasing children's happiness and health, and indirectly involves strengthening the impetus for national rejuvenation. But how do we accomplish this significant meaning? Simply put, through children's education. At the beginning of this Children's Year, we, as children's teachers, who spend our days with these innocent and lovely young friends, bear a heavy responsibility. In order to genuinely promote children's welfare, we have specifically developed this teaching outline to facilitate its implementation.

(2) Objectives: (1) To forge healthy bodies for children; (2) To cultivate excellent character in children; (3) To enhance children's essential knowledge and skills; (4) To foster children's ability to participate in life activities; (5) To understand the position of Chinese children; (6) To understand the general conditions of domestic and foreign children; (7) To understand one's own developmental sequence; (8) To enable children to understand natural phenomena and social organization; (9) To develop the ability to adapt to the environment; (10) To encourage children to practice new life.

(3) Credos: (1) We firmly believe that the 20th century is the century of the children's rights movement; (2) We firmly believe that children are the future masters of China; (3) We firmly believe that Children's Year is the prelude to children's happiness; (4) We firmly believe that Children's Year is a year of effort for all children in the country; (5) We firmly believe that new children will create a new China; (6) We firmly believe that a sound country must have sound children; (7) We firmly believe that only diligent teachers can create a happy Children's Year.

(4) Teaching Outline: (A) Activities: (1) Hold speech contests; (2) Publish special issues of Children's Year publications; (3) Hold toy exhibitions; (4) Exhibit achievements in various subjects; (5) Hold reading competitions; (6) Organize children's science research clubs; (7) Hold excursions; (8) Regularly hold various competitions, such as ball games, chess, shuttlecock kicking, jump rope, ball dribbling, etc.; (9) Regularly hold mother-daughter meetings; (10) Regularly hold social gatherings; (11) Hold rapid calculation and riddle-solving competitions; (12) Hold small concerts; (13) Practice emergency assemblies. (B) Learning and Teaching Activities: (1) Civic training: Earnestly train according to the full text of the ministerial training guidelines to cultivate children's sound physical condition and excellent moral character; (2) Language Arts: (a) Reading: (i) Read articles about Children's Year; (ii) Read poems, novels, stories, and plays about Children's Year. (b) Composition: (i) Draft declarations of Children's Year; (ii) Draft publicity slogans; (iii) Record various gatherings and activities; (iv) Draft speeches for Children's Year. (c) Writing: (i) Write Children's Year slogans; (ii) Fill out various statistics about children; (iii) Write letters of information about Children's Year; (iv) Other. (d) Speaking: (i) Performance practice (regarding Children's Year); (3) Arithmetic: (a) Accounting practice; (b) Statistics of the number of children in various provinces and cities; (c) Statistics of the number of out-of-school children in various provinces and cities; (d) Calculation of the specific gravity of various objects; (e) Calculation of various activity costs; (f) Other. (4) Social Studies: (a) Study the history of Children's Year in China; (b) Study the purpose of Children's Year in China; (c) Study the general conditions of domestic children; (d) Study the general conditions of foreign children; (e) Study the problem of out-of-school children; (f) Study the problem of children's welfare programs; (g) Study the Geneva Declaration of the Rights of the Child. (5) Natural Science: (a) Study developmental processes; (b) Study children's clothing, food, housing, and transportation; (c) Study knowledge and skills for using nature to solve life problems; (d) Other. (6) Hygiene: Study children's health problems; (b) Implement the Ten Commandments of Children's Hygiene; (c) Study disease and medicine; (d) Other. (7) Manual Arts: (a) Make simple toys; (b) Make gathering supplies; (c) Create gathering invitations; (d) Other. (8) Art: (a) Draw decorations on invitations; (b) Draw decorations on slogans; (c) Create various forms; (d) Propaganda posters. (9) Physical Education: (a) Practice children's fitness exercises; (b) Practice martial arts; (c) Scout training; (d) Play various games beneficial to children's physical and mental health. (10) Music: (a) Sing Children's Year songs; (b) Perform Children's Year operas; (c) Practice songs for concerts; (d) Children's New Life Movement Song. (5) Implementation Steps and Methods: (1) Generate motivation: Use appropriate opportunities with speeches or stories to generate interest; (2) Environmental arrangement: (a) Pictures (examples): 1. Children's work picture; 2. Children's games picture; 3. Hygiene habits picture; 4. Portraits of great people; 5. Others. (b) Slogans (examples): 1. Childhood is the golden age of life; 2. A sound country must have sound children; 3. New children create a new China; 4. Love the nation, love the country; 5. To save the country, you must study; studying is saving the country; 6. Have a scientific mind and a healthy body; 7. Have a scientific mind and a healthy body; (3) Conduct various activities based on the items in this outline; (4) Thoroughly train on the items in this outline for learning and teaching and make connections with other subjects; (5) Performance evaluation: Competitions, tests, etc., should be conducted according to the nature of each subject and various activities; (6) Implementation period: After this outline is officially announced, each school will determine its own schedule.

First Meeting of the Middle School Normal School Education Research Association's Curriculum and Teaching Group

It was decided to divide into three subgroups to study and schedule subgroup meetings for the 29th

The Curriculum and Teaching Group of the Municipal Middle School Normal School Education Research Association, after deciding to divide into subgroups for study, held its first meeting yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM at the Lake Society on Guizhou Road. Wu Yan Yin of the Ministry of Education and Li Pengfei of the Education Bureau were also in attendance. The details are recorded as follows:

Attending Members:

Liao Maoru, Shen Tilan, Tao Guangchuan, Wang Yuxiang, Sheng Zhensheng, Han Juemin, Jin Tongzhang, Wu Zhiqian, Yan Junxuan, Ji Da, Cheng Kuanzheng, Wang Zhenshan, Chen Hongbi, Li Xubin, Huang Daping, Zhang He, Cao Yuanjun, Li Baozhen, Wang Fenggu, etc. Chairman: Liao Maoru; Recorder: Shen Tilan.

Review of Issues:

The meeting began with customary formalities, followed by a review of the research issues, including: (1) Issues not proposed for research: how to standardize the progress of English teaching in junior high school, how to completely revise the overly complex and rigid middle school curriculum so as not to stifle students' individuality and enable them to achieve their potential; (2) Issues for combined discussion: whether and how to revise the normal school curriculum, the table of teaching hours for normal school subjects; (3) Issues to be submitted to the Moral and Military Training Group: how to connect students' school life with actual social life; (4) Issues to be submitted to the Funding and Equipment Group: how to find ways to redraw and print teaching charts for subjects such as junior high school biology, hygiene, history, and geography based on the new curriculum standards to facilitate teaching; (5) Issues to be studied jointly with the Moral Training Group: how to implement sex education.

Subgroup Assignments:

It was then decided to divide into (1) Middle School Curriculum, (2) Middle School Subject Teaching, (3) Normal School Curriculum and Teaching. Group 1 includes issues 2, 3, 6, 13, 18, 20, 21, 22, 27, 29; Group 2 includes issues 4, 5, 7, 8, 10, 15, 19, 24, 25, 26; Group 3 includes issues 11, 16, 28. The members assigned to Group 1 are Shen Tilan, Han Juemin, Wu Cuilun, Wu Zhiqian, Yan Junxuan, Cheng Kuanzheng, Wang Zhenshan, Li Xubin, Huang Daping, and Li Baozhen. The members assigned to Group 2 are Liao Maoru, Tao Guangchuan, Jin Yuezhang, Li Da, Chen Hongbi, Zhang He, and Cao Yuanjun. The members assigned to Group 3 are Sheng Zhensheng and Wang Yuxiang. Cheng Kuanzheng was elected as the convener of Group 1, Liao Maoru as the convener of Group 2, and Sheng Zhensheng as the convener of Group 3.

Research Methods:

Next, research methods were discussed: (1) Investigate the actual situation of each school; (2) Solicit opinions from all parties; (3) Teachers from each school will conduct preliminary research; (4) The Education Bureau will convene specialist teachers from each school to hold a meeting for review and discussion. It was finally decided that the next meeting would be held on December 13th at 4:00 PM, and the subgroup meetings would be held on the 19th of this month.
